BMC Bioinformatics 9, 18 (2008)." href="/articles/s41586-020-2947-8#ref-CR49" id="ref-link-section-d53489e2053">49</a></sup>, a program that scans the genome for LTR retrotransposon specific structural hallmarks, such as long terminal repeats, RNA cognate primer binding sites and target site duplications. LTRharvest (included in genometools 1.5.9) was run with the following parameter settings: âoverlaps best -seed 30 -minlenltr 100 -maxlenltr 2000 -mindistltr 3000 -maxdistltr 25000 -similar 85 -mintsd 4 -maxtsd 20 -motif tgca -motifmis 1 -vic 60 -xdrop 5 -mat 2 -mis -2 -ins -3 -del -3â. All candidates were annotated for PfamA domains using hmmer3 (<a href="http://hmmer.org">http://hmmer.org</a>, version 3.1b2) and filtered to remove false positives. The inner domain order served as a criterion for the LTR-retrotransposon superfamily classification into either Gypsy or Copia. In the cases of insufficient domain information, the elements were assigned as still undetermined.</p><p>Most of the transposons insert at random locations leading to novel and usually unique sequence stretches at both borders around the inserted element and the neighbouring original sequence. The de novo detected full-length LTR set provides defined element borders, a prerequisite for the exact positioning of transposable element junctions. We used 100-bp single transposable element junctions with 50 bp outside and 50 bp inside the element from both sides of the element and merged them to 200 bp joined junctions per element. Junctions from the reverse strand were reverse-complemented. The 200-bp joined junctions from all 20 lines were clustered with vmatch dbcluster (<a href="http://www.vmatch.de">http://www.vmatch.de</a>, version 2.3.0) at 98% identity and 98% mutual length coverage (command-line parameters: 98 98 -e 2 -l 98 -d). About 97% of the clusters belonged to the 1:1 type with a maximum of 1 member per line and were used for the downstream analyses. Using the above-described 200-bp joined junctions instead of full sequences reduces the amount of data for clustering to 2%, from about 10 kb to 200 bp per full-length LTR element, thus allowing a sequence clustering of 2.2 million elements in the first place. By including sequence information outside of the element, the repetitiveness of high-copy transposable element families is removed and at the same time the syntenic context is provided even for elements located on chrUn (that is, not assigned to chromosomal pseudomolecules).</p><h3 class="c-article__sub-heading c-article__sub-heading--divider" id="Sec13">PAV detection and validation</h3><p>Owing to higher sensitivity in detecting deletions over insertions, a paired genome alignment strategy was used in which each assembly was aligned to reference genome Morex reciprocally by treating Morex as a query and reference using Minimap2 (v.2.17)<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 50" title="Li, H. Minimap2: pairwise alignment for nucleotide sequences. Bioinformatics 34, 3094â3100 (2018)." href="/articles/s41586-020-2947-8#ref-CR50" id="ref-link-section-d53489e2082">50</a></sup>. From these two alignments, insertion and deletions were called using Assemblytics (v.1.2.1)<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 26" title="Nattestad, M. &amp; Schatz, M. C. Assemblytics: a web analytics tool for the detection of variants from an assembly. Bioinformatics 32, 3021â3023 (2016)." href="/articles/s41586-020-2947-8#ref-CR26" id="ref-link-section-d53489e2086">26</a></sup>. Then, only deletions were selected in both alignments and converted into PAVs with regard to Morex. In addition, a hard filter was used to discard PAVs containing more than 5% gaps (Ns) and nested PAVs. We used a previously described method<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 51" title="Gutierrez-Gonzalez, J. J., Mascher, M., Poland, J. &amp; Muehlbauer, G. J. Dense genotyping-by-sequencing linkage maps of two synthetic W7984ÃOpata reference populations provide insights into wheat structural diversity. Sci. Rep. 9, 1793 (2019)." href="/articles/s41586-020-2947-8#ref-CR51" id="ref-link-section-d53489e2090">51</a></sup> to map deletions longer than 5 kb in Barke relative to Morex using whole-genome shotgun data for 90 Morex Ã Barke recombinant inbred lines<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 19" title="Mascher, M. et al. Anchoring and ordering NGS contig assemblies by population sequencing (POPSEQ). Plant J. 76, 718â727 (2013)." href="/articles/s41586-020-2947-8#ref-CR19" id="ref-link-section-d53489e2094">19</a></sup>. Mosdepth (v.0.2.9)<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 52" title="Pedersen, B. S. &amp; Quinlan, A. R. Mosdepth: quick coverage calculation for genomes and exomes. Bioinformatics 34, 867â868 (2018)." href="/articles/s41586-020-2947-8#ref-CR52" id="ref-link-section-d53489e2098">52</a></sup> was used for determining read depth in genomic intervals.</p><h3 class="c-article__sub-heading c-article__sub-heading--divider" id="Sec14">
                           <i>k</i>-mer-based genome-wide association</h3><p>PAVs overlapping with single copy regions were identified by BedTools (v.2.28.0)<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 53" title="Quinlan, A. R. &amp; Hall, I. M. BEDTools: a flexible suite of utilities for comparing genomic features. Bioinformatics 26, 841â842 (2010)." href="/articles/s41586-020-2947-8#ref-CR53" id="ref-link-section-d53489e2114">53</a></sup>. <i>k</i>-mer sequences with step size of 2Â bp were retrieved from single-copy regions residing within PAVs. The abundances of the extracted <i>k</i>-mer sequences were counted in sequence reads using BBDuk (BBMap_37.93) (<a href="https://sourceforge.net/projects/bbmap/">https://sourceforge.net/projects/bbmap/</a>). <i>k</i>-mer counts were obtained for whole-genome shotgun data of 300Â diverse varieties of barley generated in the present study and previously published genotyping-by-sequencing data<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 9" title="Milner, S. G. et al. Genebank genomics highlights the diversity of a global barley collection. Nat. Genet. 51, 319â326 (2019)." href="/articles/s41586-020-2947-8#ref-CR9" id="ref-link-section-d53489e2135">9</a></sup>. <i>k</i>-mer counts were imported into R (v.3.5.1)<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 54" title="R Core Team. R: A Language and Environment for Statistical ComputingÂ &#xA;                  http://www.R-project.org&#xA;                  &#xA;                 (R Foundation for Statistical Computing, 2013)." href="/articles/s41586-020-2947-8#ref-CR54" id="ref-link-section-d53489e2142">54</a></sup> and normalized for differences in read depth between samples. The normalized <i>k</i>-mer counts were then used for genome-wide association scans using GAPIT3<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 30" title="Lipka, A. E. et al. GAPIT: genome association and prediction integrated tool. Bioinformatics 28, 2397â2399 (2012)." href="/articles/s41586-020-2947-8#ref-CR30" id="ref-link-section-d53489e2149">30</a></sup> and PCA using standard R functions.</p><h3 class="c-article__sub-heading c-article__sub-heading--divider" id="Sec15">Construction of single-copy pan-genome</h3><p>To identify single-copy regions in each genome, genomic regions covered by 31-mers occurring more than once were masked using BBDuk (BBMap_37.93)<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 55" title="Bushnell, B. BBMap: A Fast, Accurate, Splice-aware Aligner (Lawrence Berkeley National Laboratory, 2014)." href="/articles/s41586-020-2947-8#ref-CR55" id="ref-link-section-d53489e2161">55</a></sup>. Based on masking, single-copy regions in each assembly were obtained in .bed format and subsequently related sequences were retrieved using BEDTools (v2.28.0)<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 53" title="Quinlan, A. R. &amp; Hall, I. M. BEDTools: a flexible suite of utilities for comparing genomic features. Bioinformatics 26, 841â842 (2010)." href="/articles/s41586-020-2947-8#ref-CR53" id="ref-link-section-d53489e2165">53</a></sup>. Single-copy sequences from all the assemblies were combined to perform an all-against-all blast search. The blast results were filtered (&gt;90% identity and minimum 80% alignment length) and then clustered using the igraph package<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 56" title="Csardi, G. &amp; Nepusz, T. The igraph software package for complex network research. InterJournal Complex Syst. 1695, 1â9 (2006)." href="/articles/s41586-020-2947-8#ref-CR56" id="ref-link-section-d53489e2169">56</a></sup>. A representative from each cluster (the largest contained sequence) was selected and used for estimating pan-genome size. Clusters shared by all the 20 accessions are referred to as the core genome, and clusters with sequences originating from 1 to 19 genotypes are considered as the variable genome.</p><h3 class="c-article__sub-heading c-article__sub-heading--divider" id="Sec16">Hi-C library preparation, sequencing and inversion calling</h3><p>In situ Hi-C libraries were prepared from one-week-old seedlings of barley IPK core50 collection<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 9" title="Milner, S. G. et al. Genebank genomics highlights the diversity of a global barley collection. Nat. Genet. 51, 319â326 (2019)." href="/articles/s41586-020-2947-8#ref-CR9" id="ref-link-section-d53489e2182">9</a></sup> (Supplementary Table <a data-track="click" data-track-label="link" data-track-action="supplementary material anchor" href="/articles/s41586-020-2947-8#MOESM10">5</a>) based on a previously described protocol<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 43" title="Padmarasu, S., Himmelbach, A., Mascher, M. &amp; Stein, N. in Plant Long Non-Coding RNAs (eds Chekanova, J. &amp; Wang, H.-L.) 441â472 (Springer, 2019)." href="/articles/s41586-020-2947-8#ref-CR43" id="ref-link-section-d53489e2189">43</a></sup> Sequencing, Hi-C raw data processing and inversion calling were performed as previously described<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 34" title="Himmelbach, A. et al. Discovery of multi-megabase polymorphic inversions by chromosome conformation capture sequencing in large-genome plant species. Plant J. 96, 1309â1316 (2018)." href="/articles/s41586-020-2947-8#ref-CR34" id="ref-link-section-d53489e2193">34</a></sup> using the MorexV2 reference genome sequence assembly<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 6" title="Monat, C. et al. TRITEX: chromosome-scale sequence assembly of Triticeae genomes with open-source tools. Genome Biol. 20, 284 (2019)." href="/articles/s41586-020-2947-8#ref-CR6" id="ref-link-section-d53489e2197">6</a></sup>. The breakpoint regions were identified by pairwise genome alignment using Minimap2 (v.2.17)<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 50" title="Li, H. Minimap2: pairwise alignment for nucleotide sequences. Bioinformatics 34, 3094â3100 (2018)." href="/articles/s41586-020-2947-8#ref-CR50" id="ref-link-section-d53489e2202">50</a></sup> and PipMaker (<a href="http://pipmaker.bx.psu.edu/cgi-bin/pipmaker?basic">http://pipmaker.bx.psu.edu/cgi-bin/pipmaker?basic</a>)<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 57" title="Schwartz, S. et al. PipMakerâa web server for aligning two genomic DNA sequences. Genome Res. 10, 577â586 (2000)." href="/articles/s41586-020-2947-8#ref-CR57" id="ref-link-section-d53489e2213">57</a></sup>.</p><h3 class="c-article__sub-heading c-article__sub-heading--divider" id="Sec17">Resequencing, SNP calling and PCA</h3><p>Raw reads (Supplementary Table <a data-track="click" data-track-label="link" data-track-action="supplementary material anchor" href="/articles/s41586-020-2947-8#MOESM9">4</a>) were trimmed with cutadapt (v.1.15) and aligned to the MorexV2 genome assembly<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 6" title="Monat, C. et al. TRITEX: chromosome-scale sequence assembly of Triticeae genomes with open-source tools. Genome Biol. 20, 284 (2019)." href="/articles/s41586-020-2947-8#ref-CR6" id="ref-link-section-d53489e2228">6</a></sup> using Minimap2 (v.2.17)<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 50" title="Li, H. Minimap2: pairwise alignment for nucleotide sequences. Bioinformatics 34, 3094â3100 (2018)." href="/articles/s41586-020-2947-8#ref-CR50" id="ref-link-section-d53489e2232">50</a></sup>. The alignments were sorted using Novosort (V3.06.05) (<a href="http://www.novocraft.com">http://www.novocraft.com</a>). BCFtools (v.1.8)<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 58" title="Li, H. A statistical framework for SNP calling, mutation discovery, association mapping and population genetical parameter estimation from sequencing data. Bioinformatics 27, 2987â2993 (2011)." href="/articles/s41586-020-2947-8#ref-CR58" id="ref-link-section-d53489e2243">58</a></sup> was used to call SNPs and short insertions and deletions (indels). The resulting VCF file was converted into Genomic Data Structure (GDS) format using SeqArray package<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 59" title="Zheng, X. &amp; Gogarten, S. SeqArray: big data management of genome-wide sequence variants. R package version 1.10.6Â &#xA;                  https://github.com/zhengxwen/SeqArray&#xA;                  &#xA;                 (accessed January 2017)." href="/articles/s41586-020-2947-8#ref-CR59" id="ref-link-section-d53489e2248">59</a></sup> in R to obtain a SNP matrix. Finally, hard filtering was applied to remove SNPs having more than 10% missing data and heterozygosity. Previously generated genotyping-by-sequencing data<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 9" title="Milner, S. G. et al. Genebank genomics highlights the diversity of a global barley collection. Nat. Genet. 51, 319â326 (2019)." href="/articles/s41586-020-2947-8#ref-CR9" id="ref-link-section-d53489e2252">9</a></sup> were aligned to the MorexV2 reference and identified SNPs using a previously described variant calling pipeline<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 9" title="Milner, S. G. et al. Genebank genomics highlights the diversity of a global barley collection. Nat. Genet. 51, 319â326 (2019)." href="/articles/s41586-020-2947-8#ref-CR9" id="ref-link-section-d53489e2256">9</a></sup>. PCAs were performed using snpgdsPCA() function of the package SNPrelate<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 60" title="Zheng, X. et al. A high-performance computing toolset for relatedness and principal component analysis of SNP data. Bioinformatics 28, 3326â3328 (2012)." href="/articles/s41586-020-2947-8#ref-CR60" id="ref-link-section-d53489e2260">60</a></sup>.</p><h3 class="c-article__sub-heading c-article__sub-heading--divider" id="Sec18">RGT Planet Ã Hindmarsh mapping population</h3><p>A cross was made between RGT Planet (maternal plant) and Hindmarsh (pollen donor). In total, 38 F<sub>2</sub> plants from the direct cross and 233 individual heads from F<sub>3</sub> seeds were progressed to the F6 generation by single seed descent method. The F<sub>6</sub> recombinant inbred lines (RIL) (224 in total) were used for construction of a genetic linkage map. Genomic DNA was extracted from the leaves of a single plant per RIL using the cetyl-trimethyl-ammonium bromide method. DNA quality was assessed on 1% agarose gels and quantified using a NanoDrop spectrophotometer (Thermo Scientific NanoDrop Products). DNA was diluted into 50 ng/Î¼l and placed in a 96-well plate for PCR. DArT-seq genotyping-by-sequencing was performed using the DArT-seq platform (DArT PL) according to the manufacturerâs protocol (<a href="https://www.diversityarrays.com/">https://www.diversityarrays.com/</a>). In brief, 100 Î¼l of 50 ng Î¼l<sup>â1</sup> DNA was sent to DArT PL, and genotyping-by-sequencing was performed using complexity reduction followed by sequencing on a HiSeq Illumina platform as previously described<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 61" title="Akbari, M. et al. Diversity arrays technology (DArT) for high-throughput profiling of the hexaploid wheat genome. Theor. Appl. Genet. 113, 1409â1420 (2006)." href="/articles/s41586-020-2947-8#ref-CR61" id="ref-link-section-d53489e2288">61</a></sup> (Supplementary Table <a data-track="click" data-track-label="link" data-track-action="supplementary material anchor" href="/articles/s41586-020-2947-8#MOESM14">9</a>). Sequences flanking polymorphisms detected by DArT-seq were aligned against the MorexV2 genome assembly to determine their physical positions (Supplementary Table <a data-track="click" data-track-label="link" data-track-action="supplementary material anchor" href="/articles/s41586-020-2947-8#MOESM12">7</a>).</p><h3 class="c-article__sub-heading c-article__sub-heading--divider" id="Sec19">Field experiments and phenotypic data</h3><p>Field experiments were conducted at six sites: Gibson, Western Australia (WA, â33.612176, 121.798438); Williams, Western Australia (â33.577668, 116.734934); Wongan Hills, Western Australia (â30.848953, 116.756461); Merredin, Western Australia (â31.487009, 118.229668); South Perth, Western Australia (â31.991186, 115.887944); and Shepperton, Victoria (â36.487551, 145.388470). The distance between South Perth and Shepperton is over 3,300 km. The Merredin site is located inland and receives little rainfall, whereas the Gibson site receives a high amount of rainfall: the other sites are in between. The experimental design for field trial sites was performed as previously described<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 62" title="Hill, C. B. et al. Hybridisation-based target enrichment of phenology genes to dissect the genetic basis of yield and adaptation in barley. Plant Biotechnol. J. 17, 932â944 (2019)." href="/articles/s41586-020-2947-8#ref-CR62" id="ref-link-section-d53489e2306">62</a></sup>. In brief, all regional field trials (partially replicated design) were planted in a randomized complete block design using plots of 1 by 5 m<sup>2</sup>, laid out in a rowâcolumn format and the middle 3 m was harvested for grain yield. Field trials in South Perth and Shepperton were conducted using double rows with a 40-cm distance within and between rows, owing to space constraints. Seven control varieties were used for spatial adjustment of the experimental data. Measurements were taken at each plot of each field experiment in the study to determine flowering time (days to Zadoks stage (ZS)49), plant height and grain yield. In brief, heading date was recorded as the number of days from sowing to 50% awn emergence above the flag leaf (ZS49), as a proxy for flowering time. Plant height was determined by estimating the average height from the base to the tip of the head of all plants in each plot. Grain yield (kg ha<sup>â1</sup>) was determined by destructively harvesting all plant material from each plot to separate the grain, and then determining grain mass. Grain yield data of the field experiments, as well as plant height and heading data, were analysed using linear mixed models in ASReml-R (<a href="https://www.vsni.co.uk/software/asreml-r/">https://www.vsni.co.uk/software/asreml-r/</a>) to determine best linear unbiased predictions or best linear unbiased estimations for each trait for further analysis. Local best practices for fertilization and disease control were adopted for each trial site.</p><h3 class="c-article__sub-heading c-article__sub-heading--divider" id="Sec20">Quantitative trait loci (QTL) mapping</h3><p>Software MapQTL6 was used for the QTL analysis<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 63" title="Van Ooijen, J. MapQTL 5, Software for the Mapping of Quantitative Trait Loci in Experimental Populations (Kyazma, 2004)." href="/articles/s41586-020-2947-8#ref-CR63" id="ref-link-section-d53489e2329">63</a></sup>. The genotypic data, phenotypic data and genetic map were formatted and imported to MapQTL6. Interval mapping was conducted for each trait, and then the markers with a logarithm of odds (LOD) value of above 3.0 were selected as cofactors. Multiple QTL model mapping was performed to re-calculate the QTL. If the markers with the highest LOD value were inconsistent with the cofactor markers, then the new markers were selected as cofactors and re-calculated. The QTL results and charts were exported from the software.</p><h3 class="c-article__sub-heading c-article__sub-heading--divider" id="Sec21">Long-read sequence assembly of the Morex cultivar</h3><p>PacBio libraries were constructed using SMRTbell Template Prep Kit 1.0 and sized on a SAGE Blue Pippin instrument 20â80 kb. Sequencing was performed on Sequell II device at the HudsonAlpha Institute using V.1.0 chemistry and 10-h movie time. Data were generated from a total of five SMRT cells, yielding 604 Gb of raw sequence reads. A total of 520.72 Gb of this set (104.15Ã) was used for assembly (Supplementary Tables <a data-track="click" data-track-label="link" data-track-action="supplementary material anchor" href="/articles/s41586-020-2947-8#MOESM16">11</a>, <a data-track="click" data-track-label="link" data-track-action="supplementary material anchor" href="/articles/s41586-020-2947-8#MOESM17">12</a>). Previously published Illumina short-read data (ERR3183748 and ERR3183749<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 6" title="Monat, C. et al. TRITEX: chromosome-scale sequence assembly of Triticeae genomes with open-source tools. Genome Biol. 20, 284 (2019)." href="/articles/s41586-020-2947-8#ref-CR6" id="ref-link-section-d53489e2347">6</a></sup> (Supplementary Table <a data-track="click" data-track-label="link" data-track-action="supplementary material anchor" href="/articles/s41586-020-2947-8#MOESM17">12</a>)) was used for polishing and error correction. Before use, Illumina fragment reads were screened for phix contamination. Reads composed of &gt;95% simple sequences were removed. Illumina reads shorter than 50 bp after trimming for adaptor and quality (<i>q</i> &lt; 20) were removed. The final read set consists of 605,178,701 reads, representing a total of 43.17Ã of high-quality Illumina bases. The initial assembly was generated by assembling 32,743,478 PacBio reads (104.15Ã sequence coverage) using MECAT (v.1.1)<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 64" title="Xiao, C. L. et al. MECAT: fast mapping, error correction, and de novo assembly for single-molecule sequencing reads. Nat. Methods 14, 1072â1074 (2017)." href="/articles/s41586-020-2947-8#ref-CR64" id="ref-link-section-d53489e2358">64</a></sup> and subsequently polished using Arrow<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 65" title="Chin, C. S. et al. Nonhybrid, finished microbial genome assemblies from long-read SMRT sequencing data. Nat. Methods 10, 563â569 (2013)." href="/articles/s41586-020-2947-8#ref-CR65" id="ref-link-section-d53489e2362">65</a></sup>. This produced an initial assembly of 1,577 scaffolds (1,577 contigs), with a contig N50 of 10.4 Mb, 987 scaffolds larger than 100 kb and a total genome size of 4,139.8 Mb (Supplementary Table <a data-track="click" data-track-label="link" data-track-action="supplementary material anchor" href="/articles/s41586-020-2947-8#MOESM18">13</a>).</p><p>A first round of breaking chimeric scaffolds was done using the POPSEQ genetic map<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 19" title="Mascher, M. et al. Anchoring and ordering NGS contig assemblies by population sequencing (POPSEQ). Plant J. 76, 718â727 (2013)." href="/articles/s41586-020-2947-8#ref-CR19" id="ref-link-section-d53489e2372">19</a></sup> to identify contigs bearing markers from distant genomic regions. A total of 17 misjoins were identified and resolved. Homozygous SNPs and indels were corrected in the release consensus sequence using a subset of about 30Ã of the Illumina reads described above in this section. Reads were aligned using BWA-MEM<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 66" title="Li, H. Aligning sequence reads, clone sequences and assembly contigs with BWA-MEM. Preprint at &#xA;                  https://arxiv.org/abs/1303.3997&#xA;                  &#xA;                 (2013)." href="/articles/s41586-020-2947-8#ref-CR66" id="ref-link-section-d53489e2376">66</a></sup>. Homozygous SNPs and indels were discovered with GATKâs UnifiedGenotyper tool<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 67" title="McKenna, A. et al. The Genome Analysis Toolkit: a MapReduce framework for analyzing next-generation DNA sequencing data. Genome Res. 20, 1297â1303 (2010)." href="/articles/s41586-020-2947-8#ref-CR67" id="ref-link-section-d53489e2380">67</a></sup>. A total of 59 homozygous SNPs and 15,759 homozygous indels were corrected. After these correction steps, the assembly contains 4,139.7 Mb of sequence, consisting of 1,594 contigs with a contig N50 of 10.2 Mb. A second round of chimaera breaking by inspecting Hi-C contact matrices as described in the TRITEX pipeline<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 6" title="Monat, C. et al. TRITEX: chromosome-scale sequence assembly of Triticeae genomes with open-source tools. Genome Biol. 20, 284 (2019)." href="/articles/s41586-020-2947-8#ref-CR6" id="ref-link-section-d53489e2384">6</a></sup>. Published Hi-C data of the Morex cultivar was used<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 5" title="Mascher, M. et al. A chromosome conformation capture ordered sequence of the barley genome. Nature 544, 427â433 (2017)." href="/articles/s41586-020-2947-8#ref-CR5" id="ref-link-section-d53489e2388">5</a></sup>. Corrected contigs were arranged into pseudomolecules using TRITEX.</p><h3 class="c-article__sub-heading c-article__sub-heading--divider" id="Sec22">Comparison of PacBio continuous long read (CLR) and TRITEX assemblies of the Morex cultivar</h3><p>Full-length cDNA sequences<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 44" title="Matsumoto, T. et al. Comprehensive sequence analysis of 24,783 barley full-length cDNAs derived from 12 clone libraries. Plant Physiol. 156, 20â28 (2011)." href="/articles/s41586-020-2947-8#ref-CR44" id="ref-link-section-d53489e2401">44</a></sup> were aligned to the assemblies to assess gene space completeness. Only alignments with query coverage â¥90% and identity â¥90% were considered. Whole-genome assemblies were done with Minimap2. Structural variant calling with Assemblytics (v.1.2.1)<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 26" title="Nattestad, M. &amp; Schatz, M. C. Assemblytics: a web analytics tool for the detection of variants from an assembly. Bioinformatics 32, 3021â3023 (2016)." href="/articles/s41586-020-2947-8#ref-CR26" id="ref-link-section-d53489e2405">26</a></sup> (Morex TRITEX versus Morex CLR; Morex CLR versus Barke) and extraction of single-copy regions were done as described in âPAV detection and validationâ.</p><h3 class="c-article__sub-heading c-article__sub-heading--divider" id="Sec23">Reporting summary</h3><p>Further information on research design is available in theÂ <a data-track="click" data-track-label="link" data-track-action="supplementary material anchor" href="/articles/s41586-020-2947-8#MOESM2">Nature Research Reporting Summary</a> linked to this paper.</p></div></div></section>
                

                <section aria-labelledby="data-availability" data-title="Data availability"><div class="c-article-section" id="data-availability-section"><h2 class="c-article-section__title js-section-title js-c-reading-companion-sections-item" id="data-availability">Data availability</h2><div class="c-article-section__content" id="data-availability-content">
              
              <p>All raw sequence data collected in this study and sequence assemblies have been deposited at the European Nucleotide Archive (ENA). Accession codes for raw data and assemblies are listed in Supplementary Tables: Supplementary Table <a data-track="click" data-track-label="link" data-track-action="supplementary material anchor" href="/articles/s41586-020-2947-8#MOESM19">14</a> (assemblies), Supplementary Table <a data-track="click" data-track-label="link" data-track-action="supplementary material anchor" href="/articles/s41586-020-2947-8#MOESM15">10</a> (assembly raw data), Supplementary Table <a data-track="click" data-track-label="link" data-track-action="supplementary material anchor" href="/articles/s41586-020-2947-8#MOESM9">4</a> (whole-genome shotgun sequencing), Supplementary Table <a data-track="click" data-track-label="link" data-track-action="supplementary material anchor" href="/articles/s41586-020-2947-8#MOESM10">5</a> (Hi-C) and Supplementary Table <a data-track="click" data-track-label="link" data-track-action="supplementary material anchor" href="/articles/s41586-020-2947-8#MOESM14">9</a> (DArT-seq). Assemblies, annotations and analysis results were deposited under a DOI in the PGP repository<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 68" title="Arend, D. et al. PGP repository: a plant phenomics and genomics data publication infrastructure. Database (Oxford) 2016, baw033 (2016)." href="/articles/s41586-020-2947-8#ref-CR68" id="ref-link-section-d53489e2522">68</a></sup> using the e!DAL submission system<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 69" title="Arend, D. et al. e!DALâa framework to store, share and publish research data. BMC Bioinformatics 15, 214 (2014)." href="/articles/s41586-020-2947-8#ref-CR69" id="ref-link-section-d53489e2526">69</a></sup> and are accessible under the URL <a href="https://doi.org/10.5447/ipk/2020/24">https://doi.org/10.5447/ipk/2020/24</a>. Assemblies and gene annotations can also be downloaded from <a href="https://barley-pangenome.ipk-gatersleben.de">https://barley-pangenome.ipk-gatersleben.de</a>. The Barley Pedigree Catalogue is available at <a href="http://genbank.vurv.cz/barley/pedigree/">http://genbank.vurv.cz/barley/pedigree/</a>.</p>

              <p>Source code is released in a public Bitbucket repository, at <a href="https://bitbucket.org/ipk_dg_public/barley_pangenome/">https://bitbucket.org/ipk_dg_public/barley_pangenome/</a>.</p>

N.S. coordinated experiments and sequencing. M.M. supervised sequence assembly. M. Spannagl and K.F.X.M. supervised annotation. U.S. supervised data management and submission. S.P., A.H., J.E., D.X., L.B.B. and J.G. performed sequencing experiments. M.J., C.M., Y.G., C.P., J.J. and J.S. performed sequence assembly. M.J. performed structural variation and genome-wide association scan analysis. A.F. submitted sequence data. G.H., T.L., H.G., V.S.B., N.K. and D.L. annotated and analysed genes and transposable elements. S.P., M.J., X.-Q.Z., T.T.A., G. Zhou, C.T., C.H., P.W., M.M. and C.L. analysed polymorphic inversions. H.B., J.G., J.S., J.Z., C.W., G.G., G. Zhang, K.M., T.H., K.S., K.J.C., P.L., C.J.P., C.L., M. Schreiber, R.W. and N.S. contributed sequence data. M.J., S.P., C.L. and M.M. wrote the paper with input from all co-authors.</p><h3 class="c-article__sub-heading" id="corresponding-author">Corresponding authors</h3><p id="corresponding-author-list">Correspondence to

This is the original gel image from which the blue sections were cropped and used for Fig. 3. Morex and RGT planet were used as controls. All Valticky lines carry Morex allele of 7H inversion. Two Diamant lines (HOR 14972, HOR 4092) carry the RGT Planet allele, one Diamant line (HOR 2073) carries the Morex allele.     </div>
